  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_df6f5fd8-8f36-4f93-8d9f-e8b888253474'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7179035263774051253" style="display:none">When Griffin's first love and ex-boyfriend, Theo, dies in a drowning accident, his universe implodes. Even though Theo had moved to California for college and started seeing Jackson, Griffin never doubted Theo would come back to him when the time was right. But now, the future he's been imagining for himself has gone far off course. <br /><br />To make things worse, the only person who truly understands his heartache is Jackson. But no matter how much they open up to each other, Griffin's downward spiral continues. He's losing himself in his obsessive compulsions and destructive choices, and the secrets he's been keeping are tearing him apart. <br /><br />If Griffin is ever to rebuild his future, he must first confront his history, every last heartbreaking piece in the puzzle of his life.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781616956929" href="/book/show/30102870-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1568905904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15885023201976419945"><blockquote>
  <i>People are complicated puzzles, always trying to piece together a complete picture, but sometimes we get it wrong and sometimes we’re left unfinished. Sometimes that’s for the best.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I stayed up late last night to finish this book and, I confess, <b>I had chills down my spine as I came to the final page</b>. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25014114.History_Is_All_You_Left_Me' title='History Is All You Left Me by Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>History Is All You Left Me</a> is a deeply sad book, perfectly in tune with human nature and yet never manipulative as it explores love, friendship and grief between four boys.<br/><br/>Perhaps Silvera is just</span>
  <span id="freeText15885023201976419945" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>People are complicated puzzles, always trying to piece together a complete picture, but sometimes we get it wrong and sometimes we’re left unfinished. Sometimes that’s for the best.</i>
</blockquote><br />I stayed up late last night to finish this book and, I confess, <b>I had chills down my spine as I came to the final page</b>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25014114.History_Is_All_You_Left_Me" title="History Is All You Left Me by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">History Is All You Left Me</a> is a deeply sad book, perfectly in tune with human nature and yet never manipulative as it explores love, friendship and grief between four boys.<br /><br />Perhaps Silvera is just fantastic at putting himself into other people's minds, but I got the sense that this was a very personal story, told from someone who knows a lot about love and loss. The book is driven by its characters - Griffin, Theo, Wade and Jackson - jumping back and forth between the loss of Theo in the present and their intertwining histories. <br /><br />The story (or "history) is revealed by Griffin as he comes to term with the death of his best friend and first love, Theo. We soon learn that there is a complex web of relationships at play here, as we are introduced to Theo's new boyfriend from California, Jackson, and the third member of their friendship group, Wade. Theo was the group's anchor and they all find themselves confused and helpless without him - Griffin is especially torn between his dislike for Jackson and the feeling that he can relate to him most of all.<br /><br />The small, simple observations on people and relationships cut really deep for me. <b>The author manages to rip your heart out without seeming like he ever tries to</b>. It's in the little ways he reveals that past relationships are not quite over, not really. It's in the inexplicable sadness of moving on. It's in all the things the characters don't say. It's in the pretending you're fine when you're not; you're really not.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>He broke me in a way everyone should be lucky to be cracked open at least once.</i>
</blockquote><br />And yet, though this sounds so bleak, it's also balanced by its warmth, humour, nerdy references and Griffin's numerous quirks. For LGBT readers tired of gay romances being horror stories about homophobia, this one isn't about that at all - it's full of supportive parents and friends; positive representation of gay AND bisexual boys; teens having sex without shame, and with protection.<br /><br />Such a smart, emotional read. There is something so intrinsically sad about not saying what you want to say and pretending you're fine, pretending you're over someone and watching them move on without you. It's even sadder because there is no judgement - there are no villains here, just four teenage boys doing their best.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15885023201976419945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2141361230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2141361230" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2141361230?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146183" href="/book/show/30626556-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-friends-to-lovers">trope-friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141361230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10720158051218772170">I am convinced that Adam Silvera's books are far too powerful, and thus should be locked away in an impenetrable vault where the rest of us can't have access to them, because I feel like my life has been on a downward trajectory since 2016 when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not' title='More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Happy Than Not</a> and I have since stopped being a person and became just... sadness with legs. <br/><blockquote>
  <em>“But I know better.</em>
  <br/>
  <em>You’re dead, and I’m the worst kind of alive.”</em>
</blockquote><br/><em>History Is All You Left</em> <em>Me</em> is varying degrees of sadness. It's the kind of </span>
  <span id="freeText10720158051218772170" style="display:none">I am convinced that Adam Silvera's books are far too powerful, and thus should be locked away in an impenetrable vault where the rest of us can't have access to them, because I feel like my life has been on a downward trajectory since 2016 when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> and I have since stopped being a person and became just... sadness with legs. <br /><blockquote>
  <em>“But I know better.</em>
  <br />
  <em>You’re dead, and I’m the worst kind of alive.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><em>History Is All You Left</em> <em>Me</em> is varying degrees of sadness. It's the kind of book you finish and you're left with the vague sense of loss over something you never really had to begin with. The kind of book that is so devastatingly haunting no one could forget no matter how hard they tried.<br /><br />Griffin has lost his best friend and ex-boyfriend in a drowning accident, and is revisiting that place on memory lane they'd both walked so many times.... but would it still look the same?<br /><br />As I was reading about Griffin rewriting his history with Theo, I was blown away by the fact that people could have such a tangible perception of someone. That they could have myriad stories of them, an entire archive of memory. It was almost uncomfortable to be confronted with the reality that all of our actions leave footprints in the lives of other people. Just like Theo's actions had left red outlines on Griffin and Jackson's lives. It made me wish to never be the source of negative suffering for anyone, and if I were, I pray for it to be removed and replaced with lightness of being.<br /><br />Reading about Griffin trying to scramble to knit his bones back together, knowing an entire section of his soul that he'd sown to another was hanging threadbare was devastating. When you lose someone, you don't just lose them. You lose you too. <b>Griffin has lost the parts of himself that were Theo.</b> He lost the laughs and the jigsaw puzzles and the broken romance. He lost the inside jokes and the trips to the High Line and the different types of kisses that turned bitter and the time he should have wasted elsewhere. He lost, and yet everything and everyone else was so incredibly, hideously <i>alive</i>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I'll never understand how time can make a moment feel as close as yesterday and as far as years.”</i>
</blockquote><br />But Griffin learns that there is nothing pathetic about grief, no matter how small and transient people find the loss that you are grieving. You must allow yourself to <i>ache </i>even when they expect you to just move on. There is not rushing grief. It's a long process during which you will keep finding happiness, and then putting it somewhere safe so you don’t lose it, and constantly forgetting where that safe spot is. And that's what the characters do.<br /><br />Another thematic note this novel articulates so acutely is this: nothing is eternal, not even loss. Sometimes it looks like things are falling apart, when they’re really just falling into place, and the only thing you can cling to is your own resilience, your own ability to actively try and be the best version of yourself each and every day.<br /><br />Adam Silvera's characters are never the best versions of themselves, but they're always a little bit closer to it than they were when you first meet them. They’re flawed and problematic and not always nice or understanding. They take out their bad days on people who don’t deserve it and make mistakes they can’t come back from. They can be toxic and make people feel like shit. They can be selfish and sometimes, they just genuinely don’t know how to be there for anyone but themselves. But that's the thing, Adam Silvera never puts his characters on a pedestal because he knows that their balance isn’t always perfect and they’ll fall off.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Even if I only got to spend that first drive to the planetarium with Theo, he broke me in a way everyone should be lucky to be cracked open at least once. I had the privilege of being destroyed by him until we found a better, real me inside of the person I was pretending to be.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Also, I loved that one of the messages this books conveys is that platonic love should never be a runner up to romantic love. That platonic love isn’t less valid, less real or less powerful than romantic love. It isn’t second place. It shouldn’t have to take a back seat to romantic love.<br /><br />But more than anything, that <b>pride has no place in healing</b>. Being strong doesn’t translate to trying to harden yourself, girding yourself against the world. Sometimes, you have to learn what it means to let yourself fall into someone’s hands, warm and gentle. Not in the sense that your sadness is beautiful and someone will magically fix you and kiss your scars and all that nonsense. But that sometimes, all you truly need is a soft smooch reminding you that you’re strong enough, a hand helping you to scrape off all that hard and all that cold.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“There is nothing wrong with someone saving my life, I’ve realized, especially when I can’t trust myself to get the job done right. People need people. That’s that.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I loved this book, and frankly, I wish you could physically bottle your feelings for authors, and mail it to them so they’ll know the extent of the impact their books have had on their readers. I think Adam Silvera's mail box would be overflowing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10720158051218772170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1608523100" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608523100" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608523100?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608523100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15903894033331462782">SIT TIGHT MY FRIENDS BECAUSE I AM ABOUT TO TELL YOU ALL ABOUT THE BEST DAMN YA RELEASE OF 2017.<br/><br/>I sincerely do not know to start this review because I just finished reading 5 minutes ago and to be honest, I'm having trouble breathing because I'm so overwhelmed. <b>History Is All You Left ME</b> was nothing less than a masterpiece; it's enticing, it's thrilling, it's reflective, it's heart-breaking. It's everything you could possibly want it to be and more and I cannot recommend this book enough to you a</span>
  <span id="freeText15903894033331462782" style="display:none">SIT TIGHT MY FRIENDS BECAUSE I AM ABOUT TO TELL YOU ALL ABOUT THE BEST DAMN YA RELEASE OF 2017.<br /><br />I sincerely do not know to start this review because I just finished reading 5 minutes ago and to be honest, I'm having trouble breathing because I'm so overwhelmed. <b>History Is All You Left ME</b> was nothing less than a masterpiece; it's enticing, it's thrilling, it's reflective, it's heart-breaking. It's everything you could possibly want it to be and more and I cannot recommend this book enough to you all. Truthfully, I don't think I have a single negative word to say about this novel because it was almost unrealistically fantastic.<br /><br />Adam Silvera is the kind of author who you could read ANYTHING he'd written and know it was from him. Adam's personal voice is so distinctive and it was such a pleasure to see his personality shine through his words, even in the darkest moments. It's something I noticed in his previous novel, <b>More Happy Than Not</b> (also 10/10 recommend) and I'm so happy to see his individuality stand strong as he grows as a writer! There are a million and ten quotes I want to share with you all because this book showcases so many important thoughts through Adam's words, but I will be sure to gush in my spoiler-y video review coming this January!<br /><br />The characters in this book are CRAZY interesting. I think my feelings on each of them changed throughout the book, which is not a feeling I'm familiar with. There are characters I loved at first but grew to resent. There are characters I originally was indifferent to that I ended up falling in love with. Because so much of this novel is focused on the progression of the characters and what we learn about them through reading, I don't want to go into TOOO much detail. What I do want to say about all of them is that I'm so happy we got to know each character individually and not just know them as their relationships to each other. They all have their own "histories", their own interests, their own quirks, their own battles and it was so refreshing to not just know a <i>complete cast</i> of characters, but actually get to know the characters themselves. <br /><br />Griffin is our main protagonist, telling his story through "History" and "Today" as he reflects on his past with his newly deceased first love, as well as his current state of bereavement. He is a character I had trouble agreeing with at times because of his decisions, but his vulnerability was really admirable to me. His experiences with grief are extremely unique, but the world truly needed his story and I can only hope you all benefit from it as I have.<br /><br />Theo, our late ex-love (not a spoiler-it's in the synopsis, guys) is another character I struggled with, as we not only get to know him while he's alive, but we also learn so much about him through other's grieving. I have so many questions about him; his thoughts (as the book is entirely from Griffin's point of view), his motivations, and where he stands on the events of current times from where he is now. All I can say is that learning about his character was quite a unique reading experience that I will definitely take with me as I delve into to other books.<br /><br />Jackson, Theo's most recent boyfriend, is another character I find super intriguing. I somewhat resented him at first as I started on "Team Griffin" for obvious reasons, but Jackson played such a unique role in this story that you can't ignore. Whatever your feelings on him may be, he is really a one of a kind character in literature.<br /><br />Wade, I feel, is highly underrated, being the invisibility cloak to Theo's elder wand and Griffin's resurrection stone (yeah, I know y'all like that analogy). While he is not the most important character to the plot of the story, I feel Wade is the missing piece this story needed. He's real, he's patient, he's not afraid to say what's on his mind and stand up for himself, and I loved him. Total "precious cinnamon bun" alert, here.<br /><br />One of the greatest things about History is the representation. As a straight woman, I can't exactly speak for the accuracy of the 3 main characters all being queer, nor would I ever attempt to. What I will say is I read this with the knowledge I've gained from LGBTQIAP+ readers in mind the entire time, and I constantly found myself reflecting on how healthy the stories of these boys seemed, the positivity surrounding their experiences (despite the whole, you know, love of your life dying thing) and how happy I was to see sexuality portrayed in such a casual, authentic light. As this Adam's second own voices novel, I have no doubts about his capabilities to write realistic LGBT characters the way they should be written. I believe if you were a fan of the representation in More Happy, you will be equally satisfied reading the stories of these three queer boys.<br /><br />Also concerning representation and having a bit more experience in the mental health department, as Griffin suffers from OCD, I was extremely pleased with how his compulsions were expressed in the novel. It is displayed in it's true nature, Adam shows mental illness exactly as it manifests in real life. Although I have never been diagnosed with OCD, as a psychology student who has suffered from related mental health issues, there were many powerful scenes that did a fantastic job portraying this disorder. Adam can most definitely add another gold star to his "Times I've Accurately Portrayed Diverse Topics" folder.<br /><br />All in all, I am totally blown away by <b>History Is All You Left Me</b>. I went in expecting to really enjoy it, but I came out BURSTING of love. While I adore More Happy, I think History is currently my favorite of Adam's works (though my hands have also been itching for <b>They Both Die At The End</b> for almost a year now). This book is quite the beaut, and it's now at the top of my recommendations list.<br /><br />I'm thoroughly impressed beyond my highest expectations, and I cannot wait for all of you to experience this phenomenal work on January 17th, 2017. I'm so excited to share my full spoiler review with you guys early next year and just GUSHHH about all the things I loved (a.k.a. everything). I'm ALSO insanely excited to help co-host Adam's NYC Launch event for History with Michael BookLion at Books of Wonder on January 16th! (Yeah, you'll get the book a day early!) If you're too far away to attend, be sure to pre-order <b>History Is All You Left Me</b> and check out historyisallyouleftme.com to enter to win a trip to NYC for the event, courtesy of Soho Press!<br /><br />Ending statement: This book was amazing. Please read it. You won't regret it.<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this book from Soho Teen. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15903894033331462782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1690147558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1690147558" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1690147558?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146183" href="/book/show/30626556-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1690147558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7823402805694021982"><i>"Just because someone is forgiving, it doesn't make asking for forgiveness easy."</i><br/><br/><i>History Is All You Left Me</i> is Adam Silvera's second novel, and it may be even better than his debut <i>More Happy Than Not</i>. Silvera tells a story of love, friendship and mourning in face of loss.<br/><br/><b>Plot:</b><br/>Griffin loses his first love, best friend and ex-boyfriend Theo in an accident. Left behind and feeling lost and lonely in his grief, he recounts their history, their relationship, first-times, happy times and not-so-happy</span>
  <span id="freeText7823402805694021982" style="display:none"><i>"Just because someone is forgiving, it doesn't make asking for forgiveness easy."</i><br /><br /><i>History Is All You Left Me</i> is Adam Silvera's second novel, and it may be even better than his debut <i>More Happy Than Not</i>. Silvera tells a story of love, friendship and mourning in face of loss.<br /><br /><b>Plot:</b><br />Griffin loses his first love, best friend and ex-boyfriend Theo in an accident. Left behind and feeling lost and lonely in his grief, he recounts their history, their relationship, first-times, happy times and not-so-happy times.<br />We also see Griffin coping with Theo's loss and all he left behind: friends, families and a similarly broken boyfriend.<br />Personally I loved Griffin's and Theo's story and the relationship they shared. There was sweet parts, sad parts and incredibly funny parts. But slowly and steadily the novel took a darker and heavier turn, secrets came out and even though Griffin tried to mend his brokenness, I didn't like the outcome.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br />Griffin, the protagonist is a passionate Potterhead, suffers from OCD, and totally in love with his best friend.<br />Theo, is his smart, equally geeky and a lovely best friend. Definitely my favourite character.<br />Wade is the third boy in their squad, half grudgingly accepting his best friends' relationship under the promise that nothing would change if they ever broke up.<br />Jackson, Theo's second boyfriend is haunted by his past and turns to Griffin after the accident.<br /><br /><b>Writing:</b><br />Adam Silvera's writing does many things to my poor heart. He is an amazing author, who can pull off unbearably funny at least as well as bittersweet and heartbreaking. He is definitely one of the most talented new voices in YA. He is able to give his readers everything they want: feelings on a silver platter topped with countless pop culture references as well as diverse and multi-dimensional characters. His stories are original and hard to predict, though sometimes a tiny bit too heavy for my taste.<br /><br />In a nutshell: Adam is a brilliant author, which probably makes me overly critical. <i>History Is All You Left Me</i> is a breathtaking novel about love and friendship, teaching that letting go of someone doesn't always mean losing them.<br /><br /><i>Many thanks to Soho Press for providing this ARC!</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7823402805694021982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1633322474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633322474" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633322474?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=read-it-and-weep">read-it-and-weep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633322474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18412192782547398709"><i>
  <b>"I mean it: Promise me." "I promise you: I'll never die."</b>
</i> <br/><br/><i>History Is All You Left Me </i>f<i></i>ollows Griffin, a guy who is suffering the loss of his ex-boyfriend Theo, who just died in a drowning accident. On top of grieving the death of Theo, is he also struggling with his OCD getting out of hand, pushing away the other member of their 'squad", Wade, and finally meeting Jackson. The boy who stole Theo away from him. <i>HIAYLM </i>f<i></i>ollows events from both present and "history" weaving together and leading </span>
  <span id="freeText18412192782547398709" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"I mean it: Promise me." "I promise you: I'll never die."</b>
</i> <br><br><i>History Is All You Left Me </i>f<i></i>ollows Griffin, a guy who is suffering the loss of his ex-boyfriend Theo, who just died in a drowning accident. On top of grieving the death of Theo, is he also struggling with his OCD getting out of hand, pushing away the other member of their 'squad", Wade, and finally meeting Jackson. The boy who stole Theo away from him. <i>HIAYLM </i>f<i></i>ollows events from both present and "history" weaving together and leading up to the moment of Theo's death and Griffins life now. <br><br>Griffin is broken when this story starts out. He feels he's barley living and that no one understands what he's is really going through. He isn't sleeping, is barely eating, and isn't going to school. He can't stop thinking of Theo and his history. Things seems like they can only get worse when he has to meet Jackson. At first Griffin wants nothing to do with him. Things change once he starts thinking Jackson might be the only one who truly gets what going on, and figured them getting along is what would have made Theo happy. Griffin, though depressed, was still a <b>really </b>likeable character. I enjoyed his sense of humor, his OCD quirks, and how real his character felt. His thoughts were very authentic and made connecting with him effortless. Theo, though actually never alive in this book, felt it. He is so adorable and I could see why both guys fell for him. Jackson was sweet, kind, and brought a depth into the story that I wasn't expecting. My favorite person however was Wade. Something about his personality drew me in. Loved his humor, loyalty, laid back manor, and really just everything about him. I found myself anticipating the moments when he would show up. <br><br>When it came to <i>HIAYLM's </i>plot I knew two things: it would read to a T like a true contemporary and that it would be a massive heart-breaker... I was 100% correct too. There were lighter moments in the story, like the condom buying scene which has me in stitches... then there were these heavier scenes like one that came towards the end of the book that came out of nowhere! It had me balling my eyes out! I was at work reading and had to avoid eye contact with my co-workers because it was so bad and I didn't want them to know I was sobbing.<br><br><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-1O0IOAR1s1k/V0kB7JtJEdI/AAAAAAAADhA/3I8xP9dTDUwydlG61v34LQ6i01pNBw72ACLcB/s1600/crying%2B.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="240" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464403582ra/19235571.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Adam Silvera gives me hope that one day I will fully love contemporary books. He is also giving such a fresh, new, and important voice for literature. <i>HIAYLM </i>g<i></i>ave me everything I wanted and then some. This novel might be coming out in 2017, but will more than likely make it on to my 2016 favorites. If you haven't added this book to you TBR do it now.<br><br><br><b>Laughs were had, tears were shed, and Adam delivered. </b><br><br><b> Read this review and others over on my blog<br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18412192782547398709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1695799897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1695799897" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1695799897?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=ocd">ocd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1695799897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5840026857857505039"><blockquote>
  <em>This is the moment of the end. This is where we give up hope on reversing time, where we abandon finding a cure to death, where we live in this Theo-less universe, where we say goodbye.</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I never thought I’d say something like this about an Adam Silvera book, <em>ever</em>, but here’s the ugly truth: <strong>I struggled to finish <em>History Is All You Left Me.</em></strong><br/><br/>Really, <em>really</em> struggled.<br/><br/>It’s not that it isn’t lyrically-written, like <em>More Happy Than Not</em>, because it truly is—and more.<br/><br/>The writing is excellent, as is the</span>
  <span id="freeText5840026857857505039" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>This is the moment of the end. This is where we give up hope on reversing time, where we abandon finding a cure to death, where we live in this Theo-less universe, where we say goodbye.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I never thought I’d say something like this about an Adam Silvera book, <em>ever</em>, but here’s the ugly truth: <strong>I struggled to finish <em>History Is All You Left Me.</em></strong><br /><br />Really, <em>really</em> struggled.<br /><br />It’s not that it isn’t lyrically-written, like <em>More Happy Than Not</em>, because it truly is—and more.<br /><br />The writing is excellent, as is the main character, Griffin. He constantly reminded me of Aaron Soto from Silvera’s previous novel.<br /><br />Which is not a bad thing in itself, since I adore tranquil, trust-worthy, open-to-love heroes struggling with personal matters and trying to find their way… coming-of-age style.<br /><br />There is no <em>actual</em> problem I can pinpoint about this novel, though I did feel rather unsatisfied about the way Silvera explored the ‘‘mental illness—OCD’’ theme.<br /><br />I will admit that I have no close family or friends with a mental illness similar to this one, so it’s safe to say that I can only imagine what it must be like and not <em>fully </em>understand it to the core of its definition, but I couldn’t help but feel that something sounded unauthentic about Griffin’s OCD.<br /><br />Plus I think that with the theme of death, and love, and grief, and coming-of-age, and friendship… it was a little <em>over-the-top</em> to also try to develop a mental illness theme into the plot. Because the author really <em>does </em>try to develop it—it’s not just that Griffin has OCD, but it really affects his life and the plot itself.<br /><br />Aside from that, I found Griffin’s first love interest (yes, there are multiple ones), Theo, rather unoriginal. I understood how he made Griffin feel special, but so many other people can do that, if they’re willing, so Theo looked just like one of many other guys to my eyes. The secondary characters also left me feeling like I should see something more in them—something different—but I couldn’t.<br /><br />On the bright side, <em>History Is All You Left Me </em>is realistic enough to send waves of emotions through the reader during heartbreaking scenes, but lyricism isn’t enough. I’ll just say it: <strong>this isn’t a very original story</strong> <strong>and little about it surprised me</strong>.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5840026857857505039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2348348757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2348348757" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2348348757?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146183" href="/book/show/30626556-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10171516-jessica?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2348348757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18002560882888669202"><b>
  <i>‘we were something, but history isnt enough to keep something alive forever.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>once again, adam silvera has created a story that radiates gentle love and pure tenderness. and i had no idea how much i would be able to relate to this on such a personal level. i think anyone who has ever had a difficult time letting go of history could benefit from reading this. <br/><br/><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1740178038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1740178038" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1740178038?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1740178038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9976990292080054147"><b>[read 2 | June 2020]</b><br/>I finish my reread with a complicated knot of feelings. There is always a risk, when coming back to a book you loved years ago, that it won't hit the same ways. That <i>did</i> happen here. This time I was hyper aware of the intense level of problematic obsession Griffin had with Theo (and tbh Theo was self absorbed the whole time) and while I want to give space for messy teens and the way mental illness (Griffin has OCD) can dig into your life and leave wounds -- it wasn't deeply a</span>
  <span id="freeText9976990292080054147" style="display:none"><b>[read 2 | June 2020]</b><br />I finish my reread with a complicated knot of feelings. There is always a risk, when coming back to a book you loved years ago, that it won't hit the same ways. That <i>did</i> happen here. This time I was hyper aware of the intense level of problematic obsession Griffin had with Theo (and tbh Theo was self absorbed the whole time) and while I want to give space for messy teens and the way mental illness (Griffin has OCD) can dig into your life and leave wounds -- it wasn't deeply addressed. Wade plays such a huge part in the end, but with basically zero character development in the rest of the book. Griffin admits he's selfish the whole way through, but continues being selfish. I don't know. Grief is complex, this book is complex (and I think deeply personal to the author?). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I wince at the end where Griffin and Wade are discovering their feelings for each other again, and Wade's #1 idea is to start fixing Griffin's compulsions. 😐 Leave that to a therapist, thx. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <b>It is messy and raw, full of kids struggling with grief and self-destructive behaviours, and these are important perspectives to understand.</b> I just winced at Griffin being so consumed by his obsession (was it even love?) for Theo, and I feel like it should've been unpacked my thoroughly by the end.<br /><br /><br /><b>[read 1 | January 2017]</b><br /><b>Oh this was a little bit, how shall I put it?? Hmm....freaking heartbreaking.</b> And of course I love books that pain me so bless this book and the trees that were murdered to give it life. And although I do have some quibbles about it, and it was actually severely sad/depressing to read....I'm really glad I devoured this one. IN ONE DAY I MIGHT ADD. I didn't want to put it down!<br /><br /><b>L I K E S:</b><br />• <b>It's thoroughly beautifully written.</b> It has the kind of writing that is just a <i>little</i> dense to get through and I couldn't speed read but it was really BEAUTIFUL and ADDICTIVE and full of emotion and poignant thoughts without being pretentious or annoying.<br />• <b>And can I just say yay for good OCD rep?!?</b> I've read several books lately where the characters seem to just "turn their anxiety off" when it's inconvenient. That did NOT happen in this book which was such a relief. I do not have OCD and I'm not sure if the author does/does not. But as someone with anxiety, I related 100% to a lot of things Griffin goes through. It's important to find relatable books. It's important to see you're not alone and have that "omg this guy gets me" sort of moment.<br />• <b>The characters were all so real and amazing.</b> I mean, they were absolute hot messes. But that's to be expected since a boy they all loved died in an accident. Theo was Griffin's ex...but also a boy he'd never really gotten over. And I just felt the characters were all so realistic. So while, sure, they frustrated me at times: they were also real people and that's what I want to read about.<br />• <b>Nerds. Nerds everywhere. See them fly through the sky.</b> We gotcha Star Wars and Harry Potter references.<br />• <b>Everyone was also so dimensional and complex.</b> There is nerdom, puzzle obsession, making up of stories, trivia, random dance parties, and very intelligent people.<br />•<b> Also the romance was freaking adorable.</b> I mean, PARTIALLY. In the beginning Griffin and Theo are being each other's first boyfriends and coming out and they're just so sappily and ridiculously in love.<br />• <b>Did I mention I wanted to not ever put it down?</b> Because yes.<br /><br /><br /><b> D I S L I K E S:</b><br />• <b>Remember how I said the romance was "cute"??? It was also totally messed up.</b> Look when you start the book you know a few things: (1) Theo is dead; (2) Griffin was very very in love with him; (3) but they'd broken up. So get thee ready for a lot of people hooking up out of grief which is a bad idea btw, and people using each other like friends-with-benefits, which is also a bad idea btw...and lots of boys getting very very very hurt and heartbroken and damaged.<br /><b>• I also hate the trope of people breaking up for no real good reason.</b> WHY. STOP. USE BRAINS PERHAPS. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Griffin literally breaks up with Theo because he's worried Theo can't do long distance as Theo goes away to college. It is a frikkin' bad idea because Griffin is still wholly obsessed with Theo, but lowkey thinks he doesn't <i>deserve</i> Theo. I've seen this trope a lot and it's annoying as dropping your toast jam side down. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• <b>Also not a fan of how Theo treated Griffin's OCD as "quirks".</b> He constantly called them that and thought they were endearing. I'm not saying the book condoned this, but it was annoying to read. It made me dislike Theo (who was a bit of a manic pixie dream boy) quite a lot. I also have no idea why Griffin's parents didn't intervene about his OCD earlier.<br /><br /><b>It's a beautiful and heartbreaking story.</b> It deals strongly with grief and is so well written and I got really invested in the characters and I loved how it deeply explored OCD. 10/10 would be hurt and stabbed in the feels by a Silvera book again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9976990292080054147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1895615419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1895615419" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1895615419?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146183" href="/book/show/30626556-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=books-that-made-me-cry">books-that-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1895615419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6283623956495560289">history is all you left me literally fucked me up in 12 dimensions. <b>this book moved me and effected me on such a deep level I really don't know what else to say about it</b>. I read this book as part of a book club, and while I vaguely knew the plot, and had heard lots of good things about Adam Silvera - I didn't know what to expect exactly.<br/><br/><b>this book absolutely destroyed me</b> I read it three months ago and I swear I think about it <i>every day</i>. It really touched me, and had such a big impact on me both a</span>
  <span id="freeText6283623956495560289" style="display:none">history is all you left me literally fucked me up in 12 dimensions. <b>this book moved me and effected me on such a deep level I really don't know what else to say about it</b>. I read this book as part of a book club, and while I vaguely knew the plot, and had heard lots of good things about Adam Silvera - I didn't know what to expect exactly.<br><br><b>this book absolutely destroyed me</b> I read it three months ago and I swear I think about it <i>every day</i>. It really touched me, and had such a big impact on me both at the time and now looking back. I called it a masterpiece then and I still do now. It truly is beautiful, thoughtful, gut-wrenching, I love it. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"I love you, but I can't stay longer. It may be a while before I speak to you again, I'm so happy you were my first, Theo, and you were worth all the heartache. I hope I wasn't living in some alternate universe where I wasn't actually your first love, too. But this universe is the only one that matters and I have one last question for you: I didn't get our history wrong, did I?"</blockquote>
</i><br><br><br><b>in history is all you left me we follow 17 year old Griffin who's dealing with the death of his ex-boyfriend Theo</b> Even though Theo and Griffin had broken up, and even though Theo was dating a new boy, Jackson, at college - Griffin still thought they were endgame. That eventually Theo and Jackson would be over, and Theo would come back to Griffin. But now Theo is dead, and Griffin has to start over. He starts a tentative relationship with Jackson, while exploring his complicated feelings and history with Theo. <br><br><b>my favourite thing about this was Griffins character and narration</b>. Griffin is <i>obviously</i> dealing with a lot - his grief, his OCD, his relationship with his family and friends, and his new relationship with Jackson. The way Adam Silvera is able to explore these issues and tie them together is masterful - he really is an <i>artist</i> when it comes to writing the human person - including and maybe especially the messy things. <br>I also loved Griffin being in <u>unreliable narrator</u>. It allowed the story to slowly unfold, and exposed the flaws and downsides of characters and their actions in a way that was both surprising, logical and heart breaking. It feels as if you grow and learn hand-in-hand with Griffin. <br><br>The story flips between chapters set in the present, and set in the past, and I enjoyed both timeframes equally. As the past and the present time frames got closer and closer, I got sadder and sadder, and I was definitely beyond upset when the climax hit. The character development was beyond good, it really blew me away and I adored everything about Griffins growth and realisations. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504857524i/23833553.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504857524i/23833554.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>History is All You Left Me is a book that destroyed me, but also which made me feel <b>full</b>. It was incredibly well written - I went through so many feelings and emotions - happiness, sadness, grief, anger, confusion, even a memorable update when I said I "wasn't sure if I should cry, vomit or both" (still true).<br><br>Adam Silvera is the MASTER at writing tender characters who need to figure themselves out - who might be broken or damaged or hurt but are slowly putting themselves back together if they can. Griffin is a character that has stayed with me for three months, and not all characters do. And I definitely think he will be with me for a lot longer. <br><br>I adored this book so much, I just think it was so clever, so raw and so honest. I want to reread it eventually because it just meant so much to me and I just was so <b>impacted</b> by it. I enjoy many books, but not all of them make me feel on a deep - <i>this is more then just a book</i> way. But History is All You Left Me definitely did. I don't have enough words to really describe how much this book moved me, but it did and I love it. <br><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"But I'm a human too, with my own human feelings. You used our intimiate history to create a future with someone else. You used our love against me. Now I'm using your love against you."</blockquote>
</i><br><br><a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/jamieson_k/playlist/6KX1wZCmDlOHxxr3H9Zqz1" rel="nofollow noopener">spotify playlist</a> <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>History is nothing. It can be recycled or thrown away completely. It isn’t this sacred treasure chest I mistook it to be. We were something, but history isn’t enough to keep something alive forever.</blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6283623956495560289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883324726?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emi" href="/user/show/34410191-emi">emi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=i-spent-my-money-on-this">i-spent-my-money-on-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883324726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2984060537525624817"><i> 4.5/5 Stars<br/><br/><blockquote><b>I'm sorry, but please don't be mad at me for reliving all of it. History is all you left me.</b></blockquote> </i><br/>Hey you!<br/><br/>Yeah, you.<br/><br/>Do you like happiness?<br/><br/>And living?<br/><br/>And having your heart be perfectly okay?<br/><br/>Then this is <u>
  <i>not</i>
</u> the book for you, but I think you should still read it anyway. <br/><br/>Now, I have a confession, I read this book back in January. According to Google, 178 days have come and gone with this book existing in my life. And in those 178 days, I've lied to everyone stating this review was coming</span>
  <span id="freeText2984060537525624817" style="display:none"><i> 4.5/5 Stars<br><br><blockquote><b>I'm sorry, but please don't be mad at me for reliving all of it. History is all you left me.</b></blockquote> </i><br>Hey you!<br><br>Yeah, you.<br><br>Do you like happiness?<br><br>And living?<br><br>And having your heart be perfectly okay?<br><br>Then this is <u>
  <i>not</i>
</u> the book for you, but I think you should still read it anyway. <br><br>Now, I have a confession, I read this book back in January. According to Google, 178 days have come and gone with this book existing in my life. And in those 178 days, I've lied to everyone stating this review was coming and then proceeded to not write the review. What have I been doing? Probably sleeping or maybe eating chicken nuggets, let's be honest here. But today I've decided to change that, as it has come to my attention that there are people who haven't read this book yet. And, not even that, there are people who haven't read an <i>
  <u>Adam Silvera</u>
</i> book before, and let me tell you, you haven't <i>lived</i> until you've read an Adam book. Even though he only has two books out at the time that I write this review, I can confidently state that he is one of the best authors out there at the moment. And with his newest novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33385229.They_Both_Die_at_the_End" title="They Both Die at the End by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">They Both Die at the End</a>
</i> coming out in just a few short months, you only have a limited time to jump on the hype train before it's released. So why not start with this book, one of my favorite reads of the year so far. <br><br>However, as a side effect of writing a review almost 200 days late (and 62 entire books later), I remember almost nothing about this book except I cried about twenty times just during the first chapter alone. But, much like my life, we'll just BS the entire thing and hope my memory serves me correctly. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500092899ra/23297410.gif" width="500" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tucked inside this package of perfection we have <b>Griffin</b> who's been in love with this boy named <b>Theo</b> for even longer than I've been in love with this book. And, unlike most of my relationships in life, it wasn't one-sided and Griffin and Theo date for awhile. However, before the events of this book take place, Theo moves away to California to attend school so the two love birds break up. Griffin, though, knows that his love for Theo will outlive any obstacle and one day they'll get back together and live happily ever after. And he knows this, despite the fact that Theo starts dating this guy named <b>Jackson</b> in California. <br><br>Now, I know what you're thinking. This can't get any more devastating right? Well, you're wrong, because, after a tragic accident, Theo dies. And that's where the book starts. <s>Well, it starts at Theo's funeral. Not like right after he dies.</s> Leaving Griffin, Jackson, myself, and yourself a puddle of emotions on the floor. But because Griffin is having a difficult time accepting the death of his first love, he starts to bond with Jackson and connect over the love over one boy they both shared. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495422363ra/22815001.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, you might be wondering, <i>"Why would I intentionally read a book that is gonna crush my heart into a thousand pieces?"</i> And usually, I'd understand, as I don't like reading sad books either. But this is an <i>
  <u>Adam Silvera</u>
</i> book, and I'll emphasize my love for him as much as I need to in order to convince you to pick this up. And besides, a tree wasn't murdered just to become three hundred pages of straight sadness.<br><br>*Infomercial voice* Because wait! There's more! <br><br>This book was sprinkled with so many scenes that made me smile and laugh and give thanks to my youth. Because not only do we get to read about Griffin and Jackson's journey of acceptance, but we also get to view the "history" part of this book, and perhaps my favorite part? <s> or perhaps not. This entire book is my favorite part.</s> So while we have the present day when everything is sad and your reading between blurry vision and a handful of tissues, you also get the story of the year before, when Griffin and Jackson's relationship is just beginning. When they are just two kids in love. And those scenes, while they too have their ups and downs, are coated in an atmosphere of fun and youth. <br><br>Adam beautifully weaves in the two storylines so beautifully, I don't even know how he did it. That man is so talented. I need him to teach me how to write. And that's not the only thing he waves into the story so beautifully, but there are also elements of mental illness that are addressed in such a respectful manner. Griffin, the MC, has OCD. While I personally don't have any experience with the disorder, and it is one touched so little in YA literature, I have read reviews that state it is an accurate portrayal. <br><br>Let me mention for the gazillionth time in this review that Adam Silvera is one of the best authors publishing books at the moment. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461338787ra/18855779.gif" width="245" height="155" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But why give this book a four-star review instead of five if I'm praising it so much? Originally, I did give it five stars, but I went back a few months ago to change it. There's just one part at the end, one element that was added in the last few chapters, that I didn't like. I won't mention what it is, bc spoilers <s>and also I don't remember a characters name</s>, but I felt like the book could have done without it. And as much as I wanted to leave the original rating for this book, I couldn't get over it, I would feel like I was lying to myself if left the rating at five stars. <br><br>Now, I hope this review was efficient enough for being over 30 years late. If I didn't convince you to read this book, then I have failed at life. <br><br>Please read it. Do it for me. <br><br><i> This review has been sponsored by </i><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mtf7hC17IBM" rel="nofollow noopener">All I Want</a><i> by Kodaline. But maybe don't listen to that song for at least a month after you finish reading this. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2984060537525624817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">we were sent to earth for this. so everyone.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005054556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8844418898133699349"><i>
  <b> “You and I loved riding the L train together, always wondering if whatever car we were in was the exact car where our own history began, the prologue to what should’ve been an epic love story.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510492560i/24424508._SX540_.png' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510492560i/24424509._SX540_.png' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Very rarely do you come across a book that has the ability to snatch the air from your lungs, pull your heart straight out your ribs, plant a twinkle in your eye through the tears, and root itself so deep in your nervous system, that every-time you move - you move with the story. </b><br/><br/>Please, please - if y</span>
  <span id="freeText8844418898133699349" style="display:none"><i>
  <b> “You and I loved riding the L train together, always wondering if whatever car we were in was the exact car where our own history began, the prologue to what should’ve been an epic love story.”</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510492560i/24424508._SX540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510492560i/24424509._SX540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Very rarely do you come across a book that has the ability to snatch the air from your lungs, pull your heart straight out your ribs, plant a twinkle in your eye through the tears, and root itself so deep in your nervous system, that every-time you move - you move with the story. </b><br><br>Please, please - if you haven't already read this... Please do. <br><br>Given the chance - this novel will do so many amazing and breathtakingly beautiful things to you. <b><i>Please let it.</i> </b><br><br>Every page was a physical pain to turn. It sunk it's way into your bones and manifested into something ugly and beautiful and raw. This book will haunt you for a long time. <b><i>Please let it.</i> </b><br><br>In a way, not only do both Theo and Griff die in their respective manner. This book will kill you too. <br><b><i>Please let it.</i> </b><br>_______________<br><br><br><b>
  <u>history. his story. </u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510494275ra/24424646.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We were something, but history isn’t enough to keep something alive forever.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>This was the most I have ever cried with a book. I was a sobbing mess by the halfway mark, and I had to put the book down and buy some fucking ice cream to get me through it. <b>You know, it's going to be a great book when the first line captivates you. You know it's going to be unforgettable when every line after doesn't lose that effect. </b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“ I know you’re not around to live, and I know you’re always going to live through me.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I found it hard to breathe at one point. It's safe to say this is never ever leaving my favorites shelf and same goes for my heart. I listened to <a href="https://youtu.be/eYW2gJOYNl0" rel="nofollow noopener">Tougher than the Rest by Bootstraps</a> while reading this and the on-repeat soundtrack was the perfect melancholic tune that encompassed everything about this story. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“ I think I need to go back to the start, where we were two boys bonding over jigsaw puzzles and falling in love”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The one thing that killed me was the what-if's. <i>Fuck, man. </i><br>All the little things throughout the story added up and I felt so heartbroken that after everything, Griff lost his endgame. In an alternative universe, Griff and Theo are sitting with their kids and making the largest fucking puzzle there is, all wearing pirate hats.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I would sometimes find my lovesick self standing in front of the intercom, wishing I could press 2B and summon you down here into my arms.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The mental-health aspect that was touched all through the story really connected. I understood and felt the things that Griffin was going through, and his OCD was really captured through the writing. Also, the fact that in the real-world, mental illnesses aren't just something you can escape from was so heavily embedded in the text. I liked that the realism was not ever questioned. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I don’t know what will be left of me if love and grief can’t bring you back to life. Maybe I need to be brought back to life, too.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The writing. Adam Silvera, if I had a dollar for everytime your writing made my heart squeeze and my eyes water, I would be buying all 7.4 billion people in this world a copy of this book so that they too can experience this type of magic. <br>The writing was beautiful, it had an abundance of literary devices and hidden metaphors that those who want a light read would possibly miss and it wouldn't take away from the story, but those that catch it would be getting a little something more emotionally. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Love. I love you; this isn’t a past-tense love.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>My love for this story will never be lost. Just like Griff's love for Theo. I buddy read this book with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/43359632-katherine---paperbackdreamer" rel="nofollow noopener">this beautiful puff</a>, and after she finished - she told me that she was scared to pick up an Adam Silvera book after this. I could not agree more. I want more of his writing and his heartache so bad, because it's stunning - but I am scared shitless of it. How can one entity make someone feel <i>so much??!!</i><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“People are complicated puzzles, always trying to piece together a complete picture, but sometimes we get it wrong and sometimes we’re left unfinished. Sometimes that’s for the best. Some pieces can’t be forced into a puzzle, or at least they shouldn’t be, because they won’t make sense.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I am going to end this review on an even character count. I close with a heavy heart and a unique spark in my eye. <b>This has undoubtedly become one of my all time favourite books and without a doubt one of my favorites of 2017. </b></span>
