    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1711816053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711816053" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711816053?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781616956929" href="/book/show/30102870-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711816053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12816303463084014269"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>...please don't be mad at me for relieving all of it. History is all you left me.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I wasn't expecting <b>much</b> from this one because it's Adam Silvera, and even though he only has 2 novels published, they're the kind of novels that one <b>cannot not love</b>. That's how captivating and beautiful Silvera's writing is. It's gripping, convincing, intriguing, beautiful. History Is All You Left Me was something different than what I normally read. It's a contemporary, something I always have read, but</span>
  <span id="freeText12816303463084014269" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>...please don't be mad at me for relieving all of it. History is all you left me.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I wasn't expecting <b>much</b> from this one because it's Adam Silvera, and even though he only has 2 novels published, they're the kind of novels that one <b>cannot not love</b>. That's how captivating and beautiful Silvera's writing is. It's gripping, convincing, intriguing, beautiful. History Is All You Left Me was something different than what I normally read. It's a contemporary, something I always have read, but it's different. It has realistic issues like <b>OCD, loss, grief, and how someone losing someone special can affect their life.</b> <u>Forever.</u><br /><br />I really don't know where to start with <i>History Is All You Left Me</i>. I don't know what to say about this, to be honest. It's great, believe me, but there isn't much I could say because the story is just <b>wonderful</b> and people just need to read it. Griffin is trying to piece himself back together after losing his first love and ex-boyfriend, Theo, after being drowned in an accident. As Griffin is struggling with this loss, he realizes that there is no one else in the world that understands the pain he is feeling and going through except for Jackson, a guy who was dating Theo until Theo's death. Even when he thinks he can't surpass the grief he feels for Theo, the jealousy he felt for Jackson, and the fact that Theo is gone, he knows that all he can do right now to surpass this history <b>is to give out the history that Theo left him.</b> <br /><br />The book changes the perspective between history and the present, whereas the <b>history</b> perspective is about Theo and Griffin and their relationship/friendship where it mentions the first time they shared their first kiss, when they came out to their parents, when Griffin admitted to Theo that he is gay and that he likes Theo, when they had happy moments too when they broke up. The <b>present</b> perspective is where Griffin goes to Theo's funeral, and from there it goes to him talking to Jackson, learning about Jackson and more about Theo, and even forming a friendship with Jackson when he didn't think about it.<br /><br />Admittedly, <b>I don't know what it is like to lose someone so special in their life.</b> I am the worst person someone could come up to and ask for advice or comfort for this because I can't tell you "I've been there" or "I know what that feels like" and I'm not gonna lie to you, I really don't. Although I don't know what it's like, <b>I felt bad for Griffin.</b> He was struggling hard to get over this loss and people didn't understand the pain he was feeling, even Jackson at times. He came to conclusion to accepting the fact, but it was hard and took a while. Griffin didn't have anyone that could help him and he didn't want anyone's advice and help either way. I felt <b>sympathy for him</b> and I could see why he felt what he felt. He was so in love with Theo and the way he would act around him was just so cute when they were dating. The history perspectives were obviously my favorite, and I enjoyed very much reading about his relationship with Theo and the happy moments they spent together and made. <br /><br />Like my friend Amber, it's difficult to write a review for this. I'm also stuck like she was. The only thing I can really say is <b>I felt bad for Griffin.</b> Sure, I felt bad for Jackson as well, but sometimes I hated Jackson because I felt bad for Griffin. Does that even make sense? I came to the conclusion that I preferred Griffin and Theo together and I was just mad when I read the sentences stating that Jackson was dating Theo at the moment and not Griffin. <b>The story is heartbreaking yet strong, and I love that.</b> One minute I'm laughing my ass off, the other minute I'm crying tears that I stained my book. <b>Adam Silvera really knows how to keep a reader smiling tears of joy and crying tears of pain.</b> He has a unique writing style, and I say that a lot about authors because I do believe that authors have a different style of writing although some don't show it and/or some readers don't believe it. Adam is different, and I mean that. His writing is beautiful and just by reading the first sentence to the last, the reader is left surprised, shocked, and relieved because of what they just read. <br /><br />I will say that I enjoyed this more than <i>More Happy Than Not</i> because Adam admitted that the realistic facts in this book are real and come from <b>him; from his experience</b> which I found out about thanks to Amber and Caitlin's review. The twitter <a href="https://twitter.com/AdamSilvera/status/813592310818611200" rel="nofollow noopener">thread</a> is and I really didn't know about that until I saw it in their review. I love it when authors do that and they do it right. They write a story that might not be about them but include points that they dealt with, deal with, struggle with, or are trying to surpass. Adam didn't fail, and the way OCD was delivered in this book felt real as well. I have never been diagnosed with a mental illness/disorder and in no way do I make fun of it, but I have felt like I have one that hasn't been found yet by the doctors because I haven't asked them to or allowed them to and <b>because I have felt them.</b> <br /><br />Like I said, I was laughing one minute and then suddenly, I found myself crying and wiping my eyes, my dark circles because I felt tears. The book is <b>hilarious</b> but it isn't only that. It's sad. Period. I never got around into reading LGBT books until last year thanks to my friend that always took LGBT books and told me they are "good" and I'm never disappointed. The book is supportive in every way when we come to discussing homosexuality. There are no homophobic's, even at school, which was something I was glad for. There are supportive parents who loved their songs as much as they did before and basically looked like they loved them more <b>because they finally came out and discovered themselves.</b> There's the dad that sees his son at Target buying condoms and "goes with the flow" telling his son "it's good that you're buying protection" because these two boys are about to have sex. There are friends that will hang out with these 2 boys no matter where they go, as long as they aren't the third wheel, which is relatable. Overall, the book <b>leaves you in pieces and basically fills your heart but then breaks it when the author doesn't try to.</b> It all depends on the reader and the emotions one can get.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12816303463084014269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1640613526" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1640613526" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1640613526?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1640613526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16383307110936078737">I'm at about 4.5 stars with this one.<br/><br/>Oh, man, this book...<br/><br/>Theo was Griffin's first love. They were best friends first, and then one day, Theo surprised Griffin by expressing his feelings for him, especially since they had never discussed either of them being gay. (This was Theo's secret; Griffin's was revealing to Theo that he knew he was suffering from obsessive-compulsive disorder and he wasn't quite sure what to do about it.)<br/><br/>"It's going to sound stupid, and I wouldn't ever say this out loud, </span>
  <span id="freeText16383307110936078737" style="display:none">I'm at about 4.5 stars with this one.<br /><br />Oh, man, this book...<br /><br />Theo was Griffin's first love. They were best friends first, and then one day, Theo surprised Griffin by expressing his feelings for him, especially since they had never discussed either of them being gay. (This was Theo's secret; Griffin's was revealing to Theo that he knew he was suffering from obsessive-compulsive disorder and he wasn't quite sure what to do about it.)<br /><br />"It's going to sound stupid, and I wouldn't ever say this out loud, but the way Theo and I came out to each other was sort of like getting caught in a thunderstorm. Storms can suck when they're knocking out power and ripping apart houses, no doubt. But other times the thunder is a soundtrack to something unpredictable, something that gets our hearts racing and wakes us up. If someone had warned me about the weather, I might have freaked out and stayed inside."<br /><br />Griffin and Theo's relationship was truly special—they shared many inside jokes, romantic and goofy moments, and Theo tried to help Griffin deal with his OCD. When Theo gets the opportunity to attend college in California on early admission, Griffin has a feeling that being out of sight might mean out of mind with Theo, so he breaks up with him. But Griffin knows Theo is his endgame, and that they'll eventually find their way back to each other and their love.<br /><br />As Theo's first year of college unfolds, it's no surprise that he begins dating Jackson. Griffin does his best to be happy for his best friend, but he is hurting, and his pain is making his compulsions more intense. He knows that Jackson wants Theo to stop being friends with Griffin as well as their other best friend Wade. Griffin starts to wonder whether he should try and move on to, if the endgame he had always dreamed of has changed. And then, without warning, Theo drowns.<br /><br />Theo's death throws Griffin into a tailspin. He doesn't want to do anything—go to school, leave the house, anything except mourn for his true love and his best friend. To make matters worse, Jackson comes to New York for Theo's funeral and then stays for a little while, to escape from where the tragedy happened. Yet despite their mutual jealousy of the other, Jackson and Griffin start to open up to one another, since they're the only ones who truly knew Theo this way, and they're the only ones who feel this kind of grief.<br /><br />But no matter how much they confide in each other, the pain of Theo's loving someone else, coupled with Griffin's grief, is dragging him down. He wants nothing more than to shut the world out—Wade, his family, everyone and everything. He can't ignore the fact that his OCD is getting more out of control, though, and he's starting to hurt everyone else in the process. The only way he can attempt to move on is to try and come to terms with his and Theo's history, from start to finish—without varnishing over anything or avoiding the pain.<br /><br />This is an intense book, but it's not all as sad as you'd expect. I might have teared up a time or two, but I was surprised I didn't become more emotional given the subject matter. I think that's because Adam Silvera tried not to make the book <i>too</i> heavy, even as Griffin and the other characters dealt with some serious grief, as well as unresolved anger.<br /><br />Silvera is such an excellent writer. His book <b>
  <i>More Happy Than Not</i>
</b> made my list of <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2016/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2015.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">the best books I read in 2015</a>.<br /> <br />The book shifts back and forth from when Theo and Griffin's relationship first began to the present, and you wonder how everything is going to occur. I'll admit I struggled with Griffin's character a bit, because his grief made him a little too difficult to dealt with, and his selfcenteredness, while understandable, made him less than sympathetic at times. But as Silvera lets the whole story unfold, you can understand why he acts the way he does.<br /><br />I read about 90 percent of this book in a day. It's not an easy read emotionally, but Silvera immerses you in the story and makes you feel the emotions his characters do. The fact that the boys' sexuality was just presented in a matter-of-fact way, without experiencing any homophobia or people's difficulty accepting them, once again leads me to wish this type of YA fiction existed when I was a YA.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16383307110936078737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10310305942714537826" style="display:none">DNF at page 121. <br /><br />Well, that took a turn that I wasn’t prepared for. <br /><br />My history with Adam Silvera:<br />More Happy Than Not — 3/5 ⭐️ <br />They Both Die At the End — 4.5 ⭐️ <br />What If It’s Us - 4.5 ⭐️ <br /><br />So, I knew going into this, it could’ve been a hit or miss for me. As soon as I started reading it, the writing style was already jarring me and the change between the past and the present wasn’t helping. <br /><br />100 pages in, I thought I was getting used to the writing style, but there was just no excitement in picking this book up and my feelings towards it would constantly fluctuate between dislike and indifference, neither was I getting attached to the characters. <br /><br />By page 121, I was just feeling empty and wasn’t interested in continuing on, so a DNF it became. The writing style hindered my enjoyment of the book, because the story was actually great. It’s the kind of style of writing that’ll either work for you or not. And since I didn’t, it didn’t allow me to form a connection to it at all. <br /><br />My reading has been all over the place this year and so I don’t want to continue on with books that don’t have me slightly hooked by the 100-page mark.</span>

  <span id="freeText2345490396813697534" style="display:none">"I don't know if I can stand hearing about your happiness with him, but maybe it'll<br />help me understand you better. Maybe it'll help me add pieces to the puzzle of your life."<br /><br />Theo and Griffin - best friends since grade school - became 'boyfriends' when they were sixteen. Both with wonderful supportive parents...I laughed when Griffin's dad said..."That's wonderful, but no more sleepovers". <br />Soon, in a very funny scene, Griffin and Theo run into Griffin's dad while in a drug store. Busted, Griffin is holding a box of condoms and a bag of gummy bears. <br />Griffin thought he'd rather be caught masturbating than this embarrassment.... but 'cool dad'..... ( after a 'little' pause reaction of course), just says...."protection is important". <br />After an enlightening dialogue about the BEES &amp; the BEES, Dad paid for those condoms with the items he was purchasing. The boys being gay - was so wonderfully natural,.... it was the smallest part of the story! Kudos to the author for gay being a non-issue-gender-issue. <br /><br />When Theo dies in a drowning accident, Griffin's universe is shattered. <br />Jackson may be the new boyfriend.....but in Griffin's thinking, he had the longest 'love' history. FIRST LOVE is something 'very special'. He rules, and doesn't want to share his loss with some 'California boyfriend' Geeeezzzz! <br /><br />Griffin meets Jackson at Theo's funeral in New York. <br />New-boyfriend, Theo, went to college with Jackson in California. <br />At first - I'm sure Griffin wanted to throw darts in Jackson's eyes... but it didn't take long for Griffin to have a change of heart about speaking with Jackson.<br />Griffin says:<br />"But now--as vulnerable or pathetic as this sounds --Jackson is someone I'm turning to. I'm not strong enough to suffer alone." <br /><br />Author Adam Silvera alternates between the HISTORY and THE PRESENT.....through the eyes of Griffin. The grieving process takes on a life of its own-- with some surprising turns towards the end. <br /><br />First rate writing- a gem of a story!!! <br /><br />Themes explored are friendships, love, loss, grief, OCD, death, memories, laughter, fun times, faith, lies &amp; honesty, with lots of warmth and tenderness!!</span>

    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1840639671?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>

          marked it as dnf

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1840639671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7306942277586137970">I had a feeling before I started this that it wouldn't be my thing. I don't read a lot of YA, and especially don't read a lot of YA contemporary. But I wanted to give it a chance because it was part of <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wXPII6N8ySw' rel='nofollow noopener'>my 2017 BookTube Recommends project</a>. However, after reading 25% of the book I know it's not my jam. I couldn't click with the writing style, especially the switching back and forth of the 1st person and 2nd person tenses between chapters. I might've been able to spend a few more hours and finished</span>
  <span id="freeText7306942277586137970" style="display:none">I had a feeling before I started this that it wouldn't be my thing. I don't read a lot of YA, and especially don't read a lot of YA contemporary. But I wanted to give it a chance because it was part of <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wXPII6N8ySw" rel="nofollow noopener">my 2017 BookTube Recommends project</a>. However, after reading 25% of the book I know it's not my jam. I couldn't click with the writing style, especially the switching back and forth of the 1st person and 2nd person tenses between chapters. I might've been able to spend a few more hours and finished this one, but I would rather DNF than force myself to keep reading and then end up giving it a low rating. That's not fair to the author, and that's not fair to people who read my reviews since I knew from early on that I wasn't liking this. That isn't to say other people won't enjoy this one. In fact, I know a ton of people who <i>love</i> this book, and I'm glad that they do because it tackles some really important topics and seems to do a good job handling them. I just couldn't bring myself to get into the story and didn't want to force it.</span>

<div id="review_1867162918" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1867162918" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1867162918?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781616956929" href="/book/show/30102870-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1867162918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6070896683672090708"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm sorry, but please don't be mad at me for reliving all of it. History is all you left me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br/>Oh, where to start with this one. I have a <i>lot</i> of feelings about this book, and I guess I’ll just go ahead and get this out of the way: despite the fact that I still gave it a decent rating, I’m tremendously disappointed, because I thought for sure that this would be a 5-star read for me. I adored Adam’s most recent release, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922965906' rel='nofollow noopener'>They Both Die at the End</a>
</i>, to the degree that I put him on my a</span>
  <span id="freeText6070896683672090708" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm sorry, but please don't be mad at me for reliving all of it. History is all you left me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br />Oh, where to start with this one. I have a <i>lot</i> of feelings about this book, and I guess I’ll just go ahead and get this out of the way: despite the fact that I still gave it a decent rating, I’m tremendously disappointed, because I thought for sure that this would be a 5-star read for me. I adored Adam’s most recent release, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922965906" rel="nofollow noopener">They Both Die at the End</a>
</i>, to the degree that I put him on my auto-buy list immediately. I’d heard such good things about <i>History</i> that I went into it fully convinced it would be just as good, but that wasn’t entirely the case.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I was in love and love died and the pain you've left isn't pain I can see myself having the strength to face again.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />First of all, Adam’s <i>writing</i> is not to blame here. I think he’s a magnificent storyteller; his voice is powerful and relentless, his books are filled to the brim with lovable quotes and moments that you just have to stop and soak in for a moment, and his plots are devastating, haunting, and downright beautiful. The <i>story</i> was not the problem. Griffin was.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“History remains with the people who will appreciate it most.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Griffin, in theory, should’ve been a great character; he’s grieving and heartsick (we stan an angsty protagonist in this house), he’s a Potter fanatic, he’s a little cinnamon roll, and he offers a portrayal of OCD that, while at times incredibly repetitive, is brutally honest and takes the representation to a degree of accuracy (for some people with OCD—not all, obviously) that most authors aren’t willing to tackle.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'll never understand how time can make a moment feel as close as yesterday and as far as years.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Unfortunately, all of the benefits to his character are overshadowed by how tremendously small his worldview is. Despite the fact that so many other people in his life are grieving alongside him, or perhaps even have reason to grieve <i>more</i> than Griffin does, he can’t possibly fathom the idea of anyone being half as broken as he is, and so he causes constant pain to the people around him. Perhaps this was intentional on Adam’s part, as a way to offer a particularly flawed protagonist, but it was just hard to stomach at times.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“History is nothing. It can be recycled or thrown away completely. It isn’t this sacred treasure chest I mistook it to be. We were something, but history isn’t enough to keep something alive forever.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Throughout the story, as we alternate timelines between the past and present, it’s evident that we’re slowly building up to a devastating confession of Griffin’s, but by the time it hits, he’d become so unlikable for me that it didn’t even affect me emotionally. I felt like I had missed something huge.<br /><br />I heard so many people say that this story crushed them entirely, that when I closed the cover with a dry eye—me, someone who cries over those Budweiser commercials with the dogs and the horses?—I knew something hadn’t clicked right. Thus, here we are, with a depressing rating that’s far lower than I thought I would ever give an Adam Silvera book, and if you’ll excuse me, I’ll be over here, moping.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6070896683672090708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1652195492" />
    <a title="Hari ~Brekker-Maresh~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh"><img alt="Hari ~Brekker-Maresh~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504482116p2/18823024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1652195492?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hari ~Brekker-Maresh~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hari ~Brekker-Maresh~" href="/user/show/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh">Hari ~Brekker-Maresh~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=conspicuous-covers">conspicuous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=cried-my-eyes-out">cried-my-eyes-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=worth-reading-again">worth-reading-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=rainy-day">rainy-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=stand-alone-novels">stand-alone-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=suddent-twist">suddent-twist</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18823024-hari-brekker-maresh?shelf=omg-endings">omg-endings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1652195492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18330805085077500850"><b>Edit: 7.25.17</b><br/><br/>Ok here I am, like two-ish days after I read the book... And I'm still dead. <br/><br/>This book was amazing.<br/><br/>If you aren't crying by <b>
  <i>sentence number one</i>
</b> I'm sorry, I'm gonna have to ship your ass to Area 51 cuz you are not. Human. <br/><br/>I dare you. Read the next sentence without crying, or least without feeling the urge to cry.<br/><br/><i>You’re still alive in alternate universes, Theo, but I live in the real world, where this morning you’re having an open-casket funeral.</i><br/><br/>Could you do it?? Doubt it.<br/><br/>I've add</span>
  <span id="freeText18330805085077500850" style="display:none"><b>Edit: 7.25.17</b><br /><br />Ok here I am, like two-ish days after I read the book... And I'm still dead. <br /><br />This book was amazing.<br /><br />If you aren't crying by <b>
  <i>sentence number one</i>
</b> I'm sorry, I'm gonna have to ship your ass to Area 51 cuz you are not. Human. <br /><br />I dare you. Read the next sentence without crying, or least without feeling the urge to cry.<br /><br /><i>You’re still alive in alternate universes, Theo, but I live in the real world, where this morning you’re having an open-casket funeral.</i><br /><br />Could you do it?? Doubt it.<br /><br />I've added all of Adam's Silvera's books to my to-read but I've never read any of them. I just didn't... Feel like it? Idk, I'm such a horrible mood reader. <br /><br />But then I read that <i>Because You Love To Hate Me</i> and his villain was great, like really really good. Easily one of my favorite stories from that book. So I decided to check out some of his actual books. <br /><br />That is approximately when I sold a piece of my soul to Adam Silvera. (The other pieces have been sold to other authors along the line, including recently, as many of you know, Victoria Schwab.) <br /><br />The story follows two timelines: The present day and history. <br /><br />Do I really need to tell you that both timelines will fuck you up majorly? <br /><br />The history deals with how Griffin and Theo met, became best friends, became boyfriends, became ex-boyfriends, and then....?<br /><br />The present day deals with Griffin's thoughts and feelings as he's grieving Theo's death. As if that's not bad enough, throw in a little bit of unreliable narration and a lot of talking to dead people and you have this incredible, jarring story that is bound to leave you in pieces. <br /><br />But I'm getting ahead of myself...<br /><br />Lemme tell you what it's actually about.<br /><br />So Griffin, Theo, and Wade are three best friends, have been since middle school. When Griffin and Theo come out to each other (IN THE MOST ADORABLE WAY EVER) they start dating, and promise Wade that this won't mess up their friendship. Griffin and Theo declare their relationship at some family event, finally coming out to both sets parents.<br /><br /><i>“We’re dating, and we’ve decided if you’re uncool with it, we’re going to live here in the trees.” The words tumble out of his mouth in such a rush that it sounds like one long word instead of eighteen separate words.<br />“No, we said we’d live on the pier,” I add.<br />Theo glances at me. “I’m trying to throw them off. I don’t want them finding us if they’re not cool with it.” He turns his attention back to our parents. “We cool?”</i><br /><br />AND. THE PARENTS WERE TOTALLY COOL WITH IT!! YES. (But no more sleepovers tho)<br /><br />All is well and more amazingly beautiful things happen until one day Theo gets to go to college a year earlier than expected. Alllllll the way in California. (They live in New York, btw.)<br /><br />So Griffin does what he thinks is the right thing and breaks up with Theo. Theo is devastated, of course. But Griffin promises this is only temporary until he gets to college as well. <br /><br /><i>I can’t predict what will happen this year, but I’m okay with more thunderstorms.</i><br /><br /><br />As they were walking towards the airport, Theo almost a gets hit by a car. Griffin knows Theo doesn't take care of himself and sees that he might lose Theo for every, in this way. So Griffin makes Theo promise that he won't die, under any circumstances. Theo agrees.<br /><br /><i>“But you have to promise me you’re not going to be stupid and walk into traffic. Don’t die at all. Okay?”<br />“Fine. I’ll never die,” Theo says, hugging me closer to him.<br />“I mean it. Promise me.”<br />“I promise you: I’ll never die.”</i><br /><br /><b>SPOILER:</b> He breaks the promise.<br /><br />A few weeks after he moved, Theo met a new guy called Jackson, who looks almost exactly like Griffin. And he falls in love with him, too. <br /><br />And since Theo and Griffin agreed to stay friends, Griffin gets to hear every detail about their relationship.<br /><br />*insert about 20 million spoilers here*<br /><br />And then Theo dies. <br />And Griffin's life is horrible. <br />And Jackson comes from California to New York for the funeral.<br />And Jackson is staying with Theo's family.<br />And Jackson wants to talk to Griffin.<br />And Griffin does too cuz he's the only one that gets it.<br />And Griffin wants to know the Theo that was with Jackson.<br /><br />*insert 400 million spoilers here*<br /><br />Yeah... It's good.<br /><br />Just when you think nope, I cannot. I cannot put myself through this, BAM. Adam Silvera ends the chapter, and we're laughing again, in the good old days. But the good old days don't always stay golden... That darkened up as well.<br /><br /><b>Super important details you should know about Griffin: </b><br /><br />•He LOVES Harry Potter, as much as Theo loved Star Wars. (Theo never read Harry Potter. What a shame.)<br /><br />The Harry Potter references in this book are everything!!<br /><br /><i>Cedric’s death is no doubt my most painful loss ever. </i><br /><br />Yes, he's talking about Cedric as in Diggory, and before you ask, no. Theo hasn't died yet. This is part of the history. <br /><br />•He has OCD, meaning he has to count off from four instead of three (even numbers are cool, odd numbers suck. Except seventeen. Cuz his birthday is May 17th and mine is May 19th, just saying.) and he always has to be on the left of somebody. Not their right. Meaning he won't sit shot-gun in the car unless he moves to Europe. Yeah it's pretty bad.<br /><br />•His parents are totally cool, including his dad. Very supportive, and more protective after Theo's death. <br /><br /><i>“I know you don’t need some birds-and-bees talk,” Dad continues. “Birds and birds? Maybe it’s bees and bees? I’m not sure if the bird or the bee is the boy in that idiom.” He gets lost trying to figure that out for a second before returning to earth.”</i> <br /><br />That particular convo happened when Griffin's dad caught him and Theo buying condoms in the store and decided to buy them himself as they were trying to leave.<br /><br />•Theo is the only one allowed to call Griffin "Griff" okay?<br /><br />•Theo loves to give him grief about shit he said years ago. For laughs of course.<br /><br /><i>"How often does Halloween land on a Friday?”<br />“More so than it lands on Friday the thirteenth,” Theo says. </i>(He was quoting Griffin.)<br /><br />•Griffin is basically talking to Theo for most of the current timeline so you're gonna be reading a lot of "you" as if his words won't cut you deep enough. <br /><br />•All hopes of God- gone. As soon as Theo died. He doesn't get why everyone tries to reference God, when they could be staking to Theo instead. <br /><br /><i>I don’t understand why he would be talking to God for comfort when he could be talking to you.</i> <br /><br />So you see????? It's hilarious. And depressing. Both emotions get mixed up and at one point you won't be able to sort anything out (I found that bawling helps)<br /><br />Jackson's side character role is pretty life-changing. Oh and he also comes with his own personal drama in the form of two best friends that are girls. Griffin meets them as well...<br /><br /><i>These two are I’m-forgetting-I’m-gay stunning. </i> <br /><br />The rest... I don't want to say it. I don't even know how to say it. <br /><br /><b>Fuck the following quotes....</b><br /><br />1. <i>You’re dead, and I’m the worst kind of alive.</i><br /><br />Go to hell go to hell go to hell.. Don't make me cry. Actually no this is what I love. <br /><br />2. <i>“Maybe if we keep letting things crash and burn, everything else is bound to fall back in place.”<br />Or maybe the fire will grow.</i><br /><br />This one doesn't seem like much... Until you know the circumstance. <br /><br />3. <i> It’s been one month since you died.<br />It’s been one month since you lived. </i><br /><br />WHYYYY DO YOU DO THIS TO ME??? <br /><br />One more thing. I really expected to hate certain parts of this book, maybe even like it more if a few parts were removed... But no. I loved every destroying second of this book. I wouldn't change a single sentence. The flow of events, the structure of the book, the words. Everything! It all worked out perfectly. And beautifully. And elegantly. And I didn't even cringe at anything, like I expected I would. <br /><br />I'm definitely picking this up again when I need a good cry...<br /><br /><b>Edit:</b> 7.20.17<br /><br />Adam Silvera? <b>Fuck you.</b> <br /><br />I fucking hate you.<br /><br /><s>I don't mean that, I'm sorry.</s><br /><br />Why the hell do you have to do this to me??????<br /><br /><s>I'm going to buy all your books by default.</s><br /><br /><i>How the fuck do <b>you</b> have such control over <b>my</b> emotions?</i><br /><br />I hate you I hate you I hate you I hate you <s>except I actually don't.</s><br /><br /><b>You are fucking brilliant and this book is fucking amazing.</b><br /><br />I wish I could tag you, or something, so you could see this. This book is easily now one of my favorites. <br /><br />I can't rate this ANYTHING below like, 6 stars. (Except GR is a bitch, so I'll be stuck with rating it a 5, which makes this gem just feel insignificant.)</span>

  <span id="freeText17141033878315059337" style="display:none">I started this book because I wanted a book that would get me in my feels, and although this got me teary a few times, it wasn't as sad as I was expecting it to be.<br /><br />There was actually a lot of depth to this that I wasn't expecting. All the characters are so flawed and it was really refreshing to not be a typical loss story. It was so much more complex than I thought it would be and I was really refreshed and impressed. Even though Griffin makes questionable choices, you still root for him. It was a story that you get so invested into the characters, and the history versus now narration of it was done so well. <br /><br />Overall, it didn't quite live up to the hype for me, but it was still really impressive quality and it was heartbreaking.</span>

A completely different read from Adam Silvera's first phenomenal book, MORE HAPPY THAN NOT, and yet just as powerful. Absolutely a 5-star read. </span>

<div id="review_1851710115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851710115" />
    <a title="Benjamin " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33085883-benjamin"><img alt="Benjamin " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603806189p2/33085883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1851710115?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin " href="/user/show/33085883-benjamin">Benjamin </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33085883-benjamin?shelf=lgbttiqa">lgbttiqa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33085883-benjamin?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1851710115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10445826735988092936"><b>There isn't a day when I don't think about this book and cry for it...</b><br/>......................................................................................................<br/><b>Just going back and remembering the moment my life stopped making sense.</b> <br/><br/><u>Happy Pride Month!</u><br/>......................................................................................................<br/>I know nobody will ever read or see this post/review, but as there's no one else on my life who would hear me either, I just had the ne</span>
  <span id="freeText10445826735988092936" style="display:none"><b>There isn't a day when I don't think about this book and cry for it...</b><br>......................................................................................................<br><b>Just going back and remembering the moment my life stopped making sense.</b> <br><br><u>Happy Pride Month!</u><br>......................................................................................................<br>I know nobody will ever read or see this post/review, but as there's no one else on my life who would hear me either, I just had the need to express how much I loved this book and how my life won't ever be the same after reading this. <br>......................................................................................................<br><blockquote>
  <i>“History is nothing. It can be recycled or thrown away completely. It isn’t this sacred treasure chest I mistook it to be. We were something, but history isn’t enough to keep something alive forever.” </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511328713i/24503609._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm gonna be sincere, I cried for a day and I even skipped school just to read this book. <br><br><b>So, let's get this done.</b><br><br>History is all you left me is the kind of book that will leave you with all types of <b>sadness</b>, that will blow your mind and will make you feel as if you have lost something or someone as if you were <b>incomplete</b>.<br><br>This is the story (or should I say history?) of Griffin, the love of his life (Theo), and the pain he brought to him with his death. (I hate you, Theo). <br><br>At very first pages, you would be able to start living the (probably) most painful moment of your life. And with this, I mean that you will literally read some of the most painful quotes from the book. <br><br>The book alternates between the <b>present</b> (today) and the past (history). Through the book, we get to know how Theo’s actions and death had left Jackson (Theo’s boyfriend) and Griffin with so many scars. They will learn from their mistakes, they will suffer but at end of the journey, they will have to heal and accept who they are.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I'm blown away by how happy you make me. Thank you for being there for me when I'm stupid enough to think I'd rather be alone.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>What makes this book different from others is the way it has of showing how we, humans, have our own ways of <b>going through pain</b>. Our own world conception can lead us to take some decisions. <br><br>Talking about the characters, I loved them all, but if I had to say which one was my favorite, I would definitely say it was Griffin. I could identify with him because I know by myself how hard is to live with an OCD, and even though I have never been in love or even in a relationship, I felt as if I could understand how much he needed <b>to be loved</b>, how hard is to be alone. I am at the same time jealous of him and happy for him. I’ve never felt what I felt for Griffin for a long long time.<br><br>On the other hand, I couldn´t understand Jackson, I wish I had, but well, that wasn’t the case and the only thing I’m going to say about him, is how <i>nice</i> he was or how he the perfect representation of maturity was.<br><br>Wade was my second favorite, he is so cute and I love him, and I’m not anything else, if you really wanna know why I liked him so much, you will have to go through the sense of loss I went through. <br>A well, we finally have our freaking Theo. What can I say about him if not that I hate him, but I know I shouldn’t cause if it weren’t for him, I wouldn’t have been able to read this gorgeous story. I will call him <i>“Theo, Lord of the Pain”</i> for the rest of my entire life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“People are complicated puzzles, always trying to piece together a complete picture, but sometimes we get it wrong and sometimes we’re left unfinished. Sometimes that’s for the best. Some pieces can’t be forced into a puzzle, or at least they shouldn’t be because they won’t make sense.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516930326i/24930832._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think there’s nothing left to say, or rather there’s nothing more I should say. You just gotta go to the bookstore 'cause you can't keep living if you haven't read it. And of course, if you’ve already read it and you are still trying to endure pain, feel free to suffer with me (I can’t do it alone).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10445826735988092936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2263161888" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263161888" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263161888?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781501938986" href="/book/show/35564009-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-four-stars">2018-four-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-audio">2018-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-ya-challenge">2018-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263161888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1465797696168424131"><b>4 stars!</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516792826i/24903011._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“History is nothing. It can be recycled or thrown away completely. It isn’t this sacred treasure chest I mistook it to be. We were something, but history isn’t enough to keep something alive forever.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><i>History is All You Left Me</i> is my first book by Adam Silvera, and let me tell you… it packed a punch. It was a compelling, heartbreaking, and beautifully written story. <br/><br/>This is the story of Griffin. It’s told part from present day, and part from the past. In the present, Griffin’</span>
  <span id="freeText1465797696168424131" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516792826i/24903011._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“History is nothing. It can be recycled or thrown away completely. It isn’t this sacred treasure chest I mistook it to be. We were something, but history isn’t enough to keep something alive forever.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><i>History is All You Left Me</i> is my first book by Adam Silvera, and let me tell you… it packed a punch. It was a compelling, heartbreaking, and beautifully written story. <br><br>This is the story of Griffin. It’s told part from present day, and part from the past. In the present, Griffin’s heart is shattered by the loss of his first love, Theo. He’s not coping well. Between his already present OCD and the strained friendship he’s had with Theo, it hits him hard. He doesn’t know what to do or who to turn to, but seems to focus on Theo’s current boyfriend, Jackson. <br><br>I had very mixed feelings about Jackson at the start. I didn’t know how to feel about Theo at times either. Still, by the end I liked Jackson a lot and the relationship he ended up having with Griffin. Theo was conflicting as well. The more I learned about his past, the more confused I was with how I felt about him. The only person I wasn’t confused about was Wade. I completely adored him. Favorite character of the book by far. <br><br>Back to Theo and Griffin. Some of my favorite parts of the story were the lighter chapters in the beginning about their past. The story of how they came out to each other and their parents warmed my heart. I loved Theo’s Star Wars addiction and Griffin’s Harry Potter obsession (I’m a huge fan of both). <br><br>I feel like this book went into directions I wasn’t expecting and I didn’t know how to feel about some of the revelations that occurred. So many times I was at a loss of how to feel… all I know is that I felt. I don’t want to spoil things, so I won’t go on about these things that came to light, but some of them shocked me in a good way, and some in a not so good way. <br><br>This book was truly emotional and gave me a lot of feels, but for some reason it wasn’t a tear jerker for me. I was expecting all these tears, but for some reason they just didn’t come. <i>History is All You Left Me</i> is a heart wrenching story of first loves, grief, betrayal, forgiveness, and friendship. I haven’t read any other Silvera books, but I will be getting to that sooner rather than later!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1465797696168424131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1928320505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1928320505" />
    <a title="abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44478099-abby"><img alt="abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597252036p2/44478099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1928320505?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="abby" href="/user/show/44478099-abby">abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1928320505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5267147552991958010">Perhaps my love for Adam Silvera's debut novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not' title='More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Happy Than Not</a> gave me unrealistic expectations for this book, but I was honestly expecting to like <i>History Is All You Left Me</i> a lot more than I did.<br/><br/>Just because Griffin is no longer dating his first love, his best friend Theo who moved across the country for college, doesn't mean that he's stopped loving him. Griffin is confident that he and Theo are the end game, and that Theo's new boyfriend Jackson is just a distraction. But then Theo dies,</span>
  <span id="freeText5267147552991958010" style="display:none">Perhaps my love for Adam Silvera's debut novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> gave me unrealistic expectations for this book, but I was honestly expecting to like <i>History Is All You Left Me</i> a lot more than I did.<br /><br />Just because Griffin is no longer dating his first love, his best friend Theo who moved across the country for college, doesn't mean that he's stopped loving him. Griffin is confident that he and Theo are the end game, and that Theo's new boyfriend Jackson is just a distraction. But then Theo dies, and Griffin finds himself lost in a universe where nothing makes sense. The only person who knows what he's going through is Jackson. Griffin and Jackson had previously seen each other as rivals, but they come together as allies in order to grieve Theo and learn to say good-bye.<br /><br />There are definitely parts of this book that are heartwarming and moving. The writing is excellent. But the story also drags. I hate to say it, but by the second half of the book, I was <i>bored</i>. Griffin reminds me enough of Aaron Soto from <i>More Happy Than Not</i> that he almost feels like a recycled character-- which means he's as aggravatingly self-centered and love obsessive as Aaron was. I couldn't warm to Griffin, and the secondary characters mostly fell flat for me, as well. A plot this thin needed richer characters to make it work. I do think Silvera is a talented author, but this story is missing the special something that made me love his previous work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5267147552991958010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1353604546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353604546" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353604546?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781616956929" href="/book/show/30102870-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-physical">own-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353604546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer496119972893765221">A poignant, heartbreaking read about grief and romance and the space between loving someone and losing them. <i>History is All You Left Me</i> follows Griffin, whose ex-boyfriend Theo died in a drowning accident in California. Griffin experiences sadness and guilt in almost equal measure, and he complicates the situation by seeking out Jackson, Theo's current boyfriend at the time of his death. Jackson, a California native and Griffin look-alike, may not be the best person for Griffin to confide in. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText496119972893765221" style="display:none">A poignant, heartbreaking read about grief and romance and the space between loving someone and losing them. <i>History is All You Left Me</i> follows Griffin, whose ex-boyfriend Theo died in a drowning accident in California. Griffin experiences sadness and guilt in almost equal measure, and he complicates the situation by seeking out Jackson, Theo's current boyfriend at the time of his death. Jackson, a California native and Griffin look-alike, may not be the best person for Griffin to confide in. But with a dismaying lack of options and a heartbreak that feels raw and out-of-control, Griffin uses Jackson as a source of support, even if their newly-found friendship leads them both to places they do not want to go.<br /><br />Adam Silvera stands as one of my favorite YA authors of this decade. With <i>History is All You Left Me</i>, he builds upon his success with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296714862?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>More Happy Than Not</i>
</a>, crafting a story with nuanced and diverse characters, a gripping plot, and a sexy and bittersweet romance. He includes so many fabulous features in this book: layered and emotional conversation between boys, sex-positive scenes in which the characters use protection, and a main character with mental health difficulties that do not subsume his entire personality. Silvera has a rare talent for delving deep into difficult emotions with a wisdom that only comes from personal experience and a profound empathy. <br /><br />My only criticism stems from one specific part of the book that I found repetitive. This series of events occurs later on, so I have to put it in spoiler tags: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I just found the continual cheating between the characters a predictable and monotonous plot device. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It felt like all of the main conflicts in this book, other than the grief following Theo's death, came from a singular <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[lack of conversation about relationship expectations, in particular surrounding monogamy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I recognize that this type of conflict does occur often and has its merits; I just wanted more variety and nuance in the climax of the plot of <i>History is All You Left Me</i>. Still, I appreciated the plot twist of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Wade also being queer. I admit that I let heteronormativity get the best of me when that took me by surprise, but I am glad that Silvera included a cast of pretty much all-queer characters, as we have so many books that feature an all-straight ensemble - and no one bats an eye at those books <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />Overall, a high-quality book I would recommend to fans of YA romance and those interested in issues of mental health and diversity. I predict Silvera will continue to climb the ranks of YA fiction and establish quite the name for himself. Glad to see YA leading the charge in regard to featuring minority characters and characters with mental illness, and I look forward to reading Silvera's next work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="496119972893765221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2462473857" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2462473857" />
    <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus"><img alt="JV (semi-hiatus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559624981p2/20906165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2462473857?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JV (semi-hiatus)" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus">JV (semi-hiatus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471146183" href="/book/show/30626556-history-is-all-you-left-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=gay-lit">gay-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=home-for-my-heart">home-for-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=best-audiobook-narrators">best-audiobook-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=made-my-face-rain">made-my-face-rain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=this-couple-stole-my-heart">this-couple-stole-my-heart</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2462473857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6104583542340933620"><blockquote>
  <i>"You kept me alive when we were apart. I promise I’ll always do the same for you."</i>
</blockquote>To forget the past is to forget a part of ourselves that has defined us what we are in the present. For some of us, history is just a mere memory of things gone by. Some desire to go back in time to change things that we wished didn't happen or something that we could prevent — painful experiences, sorrow, heartbreaks, deaths, estranged relationships, missed opportunities, lost friendships, you name it. An inna</span>
  <span id="freeText6104583542340933620" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"You kept me alive when we were apart. I promise I’ll always do the same for you."</i>
</blockquote>To forget the past is to forget a part of ourselves that has defined us what we are in the present. For some of us, history is just a mere memory of things gone by. Some desire to go back in time to change things that we wished didn't happen or something that we could prevent — painful experiences, sorrow, heartbreaks, deaths, estranged relationships, missed opportunities, lost friendships, you name it. An innate part of the human experience is the desire to erase personal history and banish the darkness into obscurity that has plagued our lives, but life doesn't work that way, so to speak. We ask the hypothetical question "what if..." as a means to change the inevitable for a positive or a more favourable outcome, thereby creating parallel or alternate universes that we can accept. That being said, we turn again to our history. Sometimes, we need to accept the things that we cannot change, but still, have the energy and strength to change things that we can. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30626556.History_Is_All_You_Left_Me" title="History Is All You Left Me by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">History Is All You Left Me</a> is a breathtaking novel! Silvera really has a way with words. He's a great storyteller who's passionate about the world he creates, the flawed characters he shapes, the magnificent plot he weaves, and the impeccable writing that captures the hearts of readers. I'm really grateful for own-voices authors. Novels like this deserve to be read because it validates the experiences that I've gone through as part of the LGBTQ+ community. I can honestly admit that I could identify with Griffin's experiences, albeit not all of it. When his first love and ex-boyfriend, Theo, dies, his world is shattered. To further complicate the situation, he turns to Jackson, Theo's current boyfriend, to pick up the missing pieces with the hope of rebuilding the puzzle in his life, but he has to confront some truths and secrets before everything falls into the right place.<blockquote>
  <i>"You left us alone. Your death made us each a piece in this awkward puzzle that doesn’t completely come together, but it’s enough to make out the image: two boys in love with someone who is never coming back."</i>
</blockquote>Told in alternating past and present, Silvera weaves a story that is unforgettable, honest, realistic, poignant, and heartbreaking. This is the kind of novel that is meant to be experienced thoroughly. Silvera flailed and flayed me that left a gaping hole in my chest.<blockquote>
  <i>"Time doesn’t heal all wounds. We both know that’s bullshit; it comes from people who have nothing comforting or original to say. But I wonder if others keep up with this lie because they don’t want to speak the harsh truth. The wound never closes and the pain remains, always piercing, always burning, always suffocating, always bleeding."</i>
</blockquote>There was never a dull chapter in this book as I was thoroughly engrossed and mesmerized by Silvera's storytelling. One minute I was smiling, then laughing, then eventually crying. I know that might sound crazy, but it's true. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532228310i/26010959.jpg" width="400" height="222" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love how supportive families and friends are — the candour and the love that they have shown to each other as well as being straightforward when it comes to safe sex. I won't deny the heaviness in this novel — it just consumes you right from the very beginning, but the truths that Silvera illuminates here, now, that is priceless. <br><br>What we've been through has shaped us to become what we are today, for better or worse, i.e. depending on where you're coming from. History/memory/past — whatever you want to call it — will always play a part in our lives. It's up to us how to turn those experiences into something meaningful in our present lives.<blockquote>
  <i>"History remains with the people who will appreciate it most."</i>
</blockquote><b>P.S.</b><br>Dear Adam, can I have my gay heart back, please? I'd love to bottle up my feelings and send it via snail mail, just so I could prove to you that you've messed me up. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532228310ra/26010960.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Audiobook <a href="https://www.audible.com/pd/History-Is-All-You-Left-Me-Audiobook/B01MZ9QIRE" rel="nofollow noopener">sample</a> and comments:</b><br><br>A heartrending, emotional performance by Tom Picasso. Distinct and exceptional characterization. Immersive narration with clear, modulated voice. What more can I say? I fell in love with his voice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6104583542340933620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3RbP1yhe8x/+csYb7g9t0L0MuhDJ9U+Q95KaT5Js7dqcP1qoK4aPiKo9mdxhAYNOrXlWJhdSFYg+sVjxtzezig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iJklW6qOlbXUML0qAiIZZeS26aYBWfF2Z+NQ0ebwGITJsLAkqVbpIoB/4u2NLPf79MMFkN/+q26uwJJvw6tG1A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera">About Adam Silvera</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1595433637p3/7577278.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15222427346673024967">Adam Silvera is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>More Happy Than Not, History Is All You Left Me,</i> and <i>They Both Die at the End</i>. His next book <i> What If It's Us</i> is co-written by Becky Albertalli (<i>Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</i>) and releases on October 9th, 2018.<br/>He writes full-time in New York City and is tall for no reason.</span>

</div>
